Applies a bone scale set to the animation over the specified frame range specified by the 2D animation curve.<br>The Input Range is the X Axis range (horizontal) and corresponds to the frame range.<br>The Output Range is the Y Axis range (vertical) and is the scale set weight value over the frame range.<br>Any frames which fall outside of the frame range are left alone.<br><center><br><img src='game:tools/images/modeldoc_editor/docs_anim_markup_curve.png'/><br></center>AnimForceBoneScaleSet nodes are processed in the order they appear under the AnimFile node and will overwrite previously written data if the frame ranges overlap.<b>NOTE</b>: Although the Input/Frame Range are floats, integers should be used. Curve data is not evaluated at run time. The curve is sampled once per frame of the animation and the values are linearly interpolated between frames.<br
Applies an animation markup over a specified frame range with a value controlled by an editable 2D animation curve.<br>The Input Range is the X Axis range (horizontal) and corresponds to the frame range.<br>The Output Range is the Y Axis range (vertical) and is the value over the frame range.<br>Any frames which fall outside of the frame range are left alone.<br><center>\n<table>\n<tbody>\n  <tr>\n    <td>Ctrl + Mouse Move</td>\n    <td>Snap Frames</td>\n  </tr>\n  <tr>\n    <td>Alt + Mouse Move</td>\n    <td>Snap Values</td>\n  </tr>\n  <tr>\n    <td>Wheel</td>\n    <td>Zoom</td>\n  </tr>\n  <tr>\n    <td>Ctrl + Wheel</td>\n    <td>Zoom X</td>\n  </tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n</center><br><center><br><img src='game:tools/images/modeldoc_editor/docs_anim_markup_curve.png'/><br></center><b>NOTE</b>: Although the Input/Frame Range are floats, integers should be used. Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>See :: https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/compressing_a_raw_clip.md<br><br>The last important setting to choose is the error_threshold. This is used in conjunction with the error metric and the virtual vertex distance from the skeleton in order to guarantee that a certain quality is maintained. A default value of 0.01cm (or ~0.004 inches in game units) is safe to use and it most likely should never be changed unless the units you are using differ. If you do run into issues where compression artifacts are visible, in all likelihood the virtual vertex distance used on the problematic bones is not conservative enough
Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>Specify how aggressively to attempt to reduce the memory footprint. Higher levels will try more permutations and bit rates. The higher the level, the slower the compression but the smaller the memory footprint. <br><b>NOTE</b>: Currently lowest, low and medium are all equivalent
Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/creating_a_skeleton.md<br><br>The virtual vertex distance is used by the error metric function. It will measure the error of a vertex at that particular distance from the bone in object space. This distance should be large enough to contain the vast majority of the visible vertices skinned on that particular bone. The algorithm ensures that all vertices contained up to this distance will have an error lower than the supplied error threshold in the CompressionSettings. It is generally sufficient for this value to be approximate and it is often safe to use the same value for every bone in humanoid characters. A value of 3cm (or ~1 inch in game units) is good enough for cinematographic quality for most characters. While visible vertices around the torso will often be further away than this, finger tips and facial bones will be closer than that. Because the compressed track data is stored in relative space of the parent bone, any error will accumulate down the hierarchy. This means that in order to keep the leaf bones within that accuracy threshold, all the parent bones in that chain will require even higher accuracy

Generates a turn layer from a 3 frame animation\n<ul>\n<li>Frame 0 :: Left Pose</li>\n<li>Frame 1 :: Center Pose</li>\n<li>Frame 2 :: Right Pose</li>\n</ul>\nIt will generate:\n<ul>\n<li>3 implicit animations\n<ul>\n<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_0 :: ( Frame 0 ) - ( Frame 1 )</li>\n<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_1 :: ( Frame 1 ) - ( Frame 1 ) - Note that this is an empty animation</li>\n<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_2 :: ( Frame 2 ) - ( Frame 1 )</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>A pose parameter named "turn" by default with the range [-1, 1]</li>\n<li>A 1D Blend additive sequence with pose parameter values [-1, 0, 1]\n<ul>\n<li>[ @_lookFrame_0, @_lookFrame_1, @_lookFrame_2 ]</li>\n<li>The 1D Blend sequence should be applied to runs with an AddLayer <img src='game:tools/images/modeldoc_editor/outliner_icon_addlayer.png' /> node</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul

Local Angles

Local Gravity CP
Local Hierarchy controls the space in which sub-frame interpolation occurs. Normally each bone will use parent space (local space) for sub-frame interpolation between two keyframes. Local Hierarchy allows the interpolation to occur in the space of a different bone or model space (world space). The space of a different bone is useful for switching the hand which is holding an objects, for example. Specifying no bone as the New Parent Bone will result in the interpolation occuring in model space (world space). This is useful if the bone becomes detached from the model, e.g. dropping a weapon. Local Hierarchy only affects how sub-frame interpolation between two key frames occurs. Local Hierarchy does not encode the bone differently at compile time
